those that operate\n    36→// on collections and those that operate on individually named items.\n    37→// Collection interfaces:\n    38→// (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n    39→//    GET: Lister -> CollectionGetter\n    40→//    WATCH: Watcher -> CollectionWatcher\n    41→//    CREATE: Creater -> CollectionCreater\n    42→//    DELETE: (n/a) -> CollectionDeleter\n    43→//    UPDATE: (n/a) -> CollectionUpdater\n    44→//\n    45→// Single item interfaces:\n    46→// (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n    47→//    GET: Getter -> NamedGetter\n    48→//    WATCH: (n/a) -> NamedWatcher\n    49→//    CREATE: (n/a) -> NamedCreater\n    50→//    DELETE: Deleter -> NamedDeleter\n    51→//    UPDATE: Update -> NamedUpdater\n    52→\n    53→// Storage is a generic interface for RESTful storage services.\n    54→// Resources which are exported to the RESTful API of apiserver need to implement this interface. It is expected\n    55→// that objects may implement any of the below interfaces.\n    56→//\n    57→// Consider using StorageWithReadiness whenever possible.\n    58→type Storage interface {\n    59→\t// New returns an empty object that can be used with Create and Update after request data has been put into it.\n    60→\t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n    61→\tNew() runtime.Object\n    62→\n    63→\t// Destroy cleans up its resources on shutdown.\n    64→\t// Destroy has to be implemented in thread-safe way and be prepared\n    65→\t// for being called more than once.\n    66→\tDestroy()\n    67→}\n    68→\n    69→// StorageWithReadiness extends Storage interface with the readiness check.\n    70→type StorageWithReadiness interface {\n    71→\tStorage\n    72→\n    73→\t// ReadinessCheck allows for checking storage readiness.\n    74→\tReadinessCheck() error\n    75→}\n    76→\n    77→// Scoper indicates what scope the resource is at. It must be specified.\n    78→// It is usually provided automatically based on your strategy.\n    79→type Scoper interface {\n    80→\t// NamespaceScoped returns true if the storage is namespaced\n    81→\tNamespaceScoped() bool\n    82→}\n    83→\n    84→// KindProvider specifies a different kind for its API than for its internal storage.  This is necessary for external\n    85→// objects that are not compiled into the api server.  For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\n    86→// the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\n    87→// API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\n    88→type KindProvider interface {\n    89→\tKind() string\n    90→}\n    91→\n    92→// ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. Delivers a list of short names for a resource. The list is used by kubectl to have short names representation of resources.\n    93→type ShortNamesProvider interface {\n    94→\tShortNames() []string\n    95→}\n    96→\n    97→// CategoriesProvider allows a resource to specify which groups of resources (categories) it's part of. Categories can\n    98→// be used by API clients to refer to a batch of resources by using a single name (e.g. \"all\" could translate to \"pod,rc,svc,...\").\n    99→type CategoriesProvider interface {\n   100→\tCategories() []string\n   101→}\n   102→\n   103→// SingularNameProvider returns singular name of resources. This is used by kubectl discovery to have singular\n   104→// name representation of resources. In case of shortcut conflicts(with CRD shortcuts) singular name should always map to this resource.\n   105→type SingularNameProvider interface {\n   106→\tGetSingularName() string\n   107→}\n   108→\n   109→// GroupVersionKindProvider is used to specify a particular GroupVersionKind to discovery.  This is used for polymorphic endpoints\n   110→// which generally point to foreign versions.  Scale refers to Scale.v1beta1.extensions for instance.\n   111→// This trumps KindProvider since it is capable of providing the information required.\n   112→// TODO KindProvider (only used by federation) should be removed and replaced with this, but that presents greater risk late in 1.8.\n   113→type GroupVersionKindProvider interface {\n   114→\tGroupVersionKind(containingGV schema.GroupVersion) schema.GroupVersionKind\n   115→}\n   116→\n   117→// GroupVersionAcceptor is used to determine if a particular GroupVersion is acceptable to send to an endpoint.\n   118→// This is used for endpoints which accept multiple versions (which is extremely rare).\n   119→// The only known instance is pods/evictions which accepts policy/v1, but also policy/v1beta1 for backwards compatibility.\n   120→type GroupVersionAcceptor interface {\n   121→\tAcceptsGroupVersion(gv schema.GroupVersion) bool\n   122→}\n   123→\n   124→// Lister is an object that can retrieve resources that match the provided field and label criteria.\n   125→type Lister interface {\n   126→\t// NewList returns an empty object that can be used with the List call.\n   127→\t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n   128→\tNewList() runtime.Object\n   129→\t// List selects resources in the storage which match to the selector. 'options' can be nil.\n   130→\tList(ctx context.Context, options *metainternalversion.ListOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n   131→\t// TableConvertor ensures all list implementers also implement table conversion\n   132→\tTableConvertor\n   133→}\n   134→\n   135→// Getter is an object that can retrieve a named RESTful resource.\n   136→type Getter interface {\n   137→\t// Get finds a resource in the storage by name and returns it.\n   138→\t// Although it can return an arbitrary error value, IsNotFound(err) is true for the\n   139→\t// returned error value err when the specified resource is not found.\n   140→\tGet(ctx context.Context, name string, options *metav1.GetOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n   141→}\n   142→\n   143→// GetterWithOptions is an object that retrieve a named RESTful resource and takes\n   144→// additional options on the get request. It allows a caller to also receive the\n   145→// subpath of the GET request.\n   146→type GetterWithOptions interface {\n   147→\t// Get finds a resource in the storage by name and returns it.\n   148→\t// Although it can return an arbitrary error value, IsNotFound(err) is true for the\n   149→\t// returned error value err when the specified resource is not found.\n   150→\t// The options object passed to it is of the same type returned by the NewGetOptions\n   151→\t// method.\n   152→\t// TODO: Pass metav1.GetOptions.\n   153→\tGet(ctx context.Context, name string, options runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error)\n   154→\n   155→\t// NewGetOptions returns an empty options object that will be used to pass\n   156→\t// options to the Get method. It may return a bool and a string, if true, the\n   157→\t// value of the request path below the object will be included as the named\n   158→\t// string in the serialization of the runtime object. E.g., returning \"path\"\n   159→\t// will convert the trailing request scheme value to \"path\" in the map[string][]string\n   160→\t// passed to the converter.\n   161→\tNewGetOptions() (runtime.Object, bool, string)\n   162→}\n   163→\n   164→type TableConvertor interface {\n   165→\tConvertToTable(ctx context.Context, object runtime.Object, tableOptions runtime.Object) (*metav1.Table, error)\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→// GracefulDeleter knows how to pass deletion options to allow delayed deletion of a\n   169→// RESTful object.\n   170→type GracefulDeleter interface {\n   171→\t// Delete finds a resource in the storage and deletes it.\n   172→\t// The delete attempt is validated by the deleteValidation first.\n   173→\t// If options are provided, the resource will attempt to honor them or return an invalid\n   174→\t// request error.\n   175→\t// Although it can return an arbitrary error value, IsNotFound(err) is true for the\n   176→\t// returned error value err when the specified resource is not found.\n   177→\t// Delete *may* return the object that was deleted, or a status object indicating additional\n   178→\t// information about deletion.\n   179→\t// It also returns a boolean which is set to true if the resource was instantly\n   180→\t// deleted or false if it will be deleted asynchronously.\n   181→\tDelete(ctx context.Context, name string, deleteValidation ValidateObjectFunc, options *metav1.DeleteOptions) (runtime.Object, bool, error)\n   182→}\n   183→\n   184→// MayReturnFullObjectDeleter may return deleted object (instead of a simple status) on deletion.\n   185→type MayReturnFullObjectDeleter interface {\n   186→\tDeleteReturnsDeletedObject() bool\n   187→}\n   188→\n   189→// CollectionDeleter is an object that can delete a collection\n   190→// of RESTful resources.\n   191→type CollectionDeleter interface {\n   192→\t// DeleteCollection selects all resources in the storage matching given 'listOptions'\n   193→\t// and deletes them. The delete attempt is validated by the deleteValidation first.\n   194→\t// If 'options' are provided, the resource will attempt to honor them or return an\n   195→\t// invalid request error.\n   196→\t// DeleteCollection may not be atomic - i.e. it may delete some objects and still\n   197→\t// return an error after it. those that operate\n// on collections and those that operate on individually named items.\n// Collection interfaces:\n// (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n//    GET: Lister -> CollectionGetter\n//    WATCH: Watcher -> CollectionWatcher\n//    CREATE: Creater -> CollectionCreater\n//    DELETE: (n/a) -> CollectionDeleter\n//    UPDATE: (n/a) -> CollectionUpdater\n//\n// Single item interfaces:\n// (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n//    GET: Getter -> NamedGetter\n//    WATCH: (n/a) -> NamedWatcher\n//    CREATE: (n/a) -> NamedCreater\n//    DELETE: Deleter -> NamedDeleter\n//    UPDATE: Update -> NamedUpdater\n\n// Storage is a generic interface for RESTful storage services.\n// Resources which are exported to the RESTful API of apiserver need to implement this interface. storage.Resource(\\\"volumeattributesclasses\\\").WithVersion(\\\"v1beta1\\\"),\\n    storagemigration.Resource(\\\"storagemigrations\\\").WithVersion(\\\"v1alpha1\\\"),\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThese overrides are processed via the ResourceEncodingOverrides field, which determines the actual etcd storage versions.\\n\\n## Configuration Merging and Factory Creation\\n\\nThe **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/resourceconfig/helpers.go** file's MergeResourceEncodingConfigs() function (lines 41-52) merges default resource encoding configurations with specific GroupVersionResource overrides by calling SetResourceEncoding() for each override.\\n\\nThe **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/storage/storage_factory.go** file defines DefaultStorageFactory (lines 61-90) which combines:\\n- StorageEncodingConfig: The ResourceEncodingConfig that controls which versions are used for etcd\\n- ResourceEncodingConfig interface: Manages version resolution for storage operations\\n\\nThe **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/storage/storage_codec.go** file's StorageCodecConfig (lines 29-39) specifies StorageVersion and MemoryVersion, which determine how objects are serialized during persistence and how they appear in memory, implementing the v1beta1-to-v1 storage version mapping at the codec level.\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe Kubernetes v1.32.0 architecture separates API version management (multiple versions accessible through REST) from storage version management (single version in etcd). REST storage providers expose multiple API versions through separate v1Storage(), v1beta1Storage(), etc. methods, while the ResourceEncodingConfig determines which single version actually gets stored in etcd. This separation allows seamless API evolution without requiring data migration when new versions are introduced.\"\n}\n","numLines":47,"startLine":1,"totalLines":47}}}
